Over there to the left ← is a snippet of the data my A.I.-powered pong player wrote to play the classic game of pong. In short, the A.I. has two major points of attention from which it learns. First, the A.I. studies the opponent ( a simple bot I wrote that uses math to determine the location of the ball on the court ). The second point is itself, the A.I. learns from its own ability to return the ball. Enforcing its succesful moves and tweaking its unsuccessful ones. Check out my github to learn more.

web dev

lunar rover

Last fall I worked on Temple University's lunar robot that competed in NASA's lunar mining competition, going head-to-head with some of the nation's best engineering programs.

I worked with four other talented software engineers. Our team tackled opportunities such as network transmission, computer vision, and remote control.

I, specifically, worked on network transmission. Turns out mars (the location NASA wanted our rovers to be made for) isn't that close. Who knew? So I made sure the data transmitted from our base CPU to our on-board CPU was smooth and under bandwidth limitations.
